# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Audit Log Middleware and Backend

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement API server audit logging: the audit event creation from requests, the audit policy evaluation, the audit backend dispatch (log file vs webhook), and the audit truncation for large request/response bodies.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Perfect! I have successfully completed a comprehensive analysis of the Kubernetes API server audit logging implementation. 

## Summary

I've identified and documented **20 core Go source files** implementing API server audit logging in `kubernetes/kubernetes`, along with **26 key symbols** and the complete **execution chain** showing how audit events flow through the system.

The audit logging system in Kubernetes consists of:

1. **Request Pipeline Filters**: `WithAuditInit` and `WithAudit` middleware that bracket the request lifecycle
2. **Policy Evaluation**: Policy rules that match requests and determine audit levels (None, Metadata, Request, RequestResponse)
3. **Event Context**: `AuditContext` that holds the event and manages multiple processing stages
4. **Request Metadata Capture**: Functions to populate audit events with request/response details and user information
5. **Backend Architecture**: A layered backend dispatch system with:
   - **Truncation layer** - enforces size limits on events and batches
   - **Buffering layer** - supports blocking, blocking-strict, or batch modes
   - **Log backend** - writes to files with rotation
   - **Webhook backend** - sends to external HTTP endpoints
   - **Union dispatcher** - combines multiple backends

The answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` contains complete details about all files, key symbols, execution chains, and a detailed narrative explanation of the entire audit logging system.

\"staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go\",\n      \"symbol\": \"ProcessEvents\"\n    },\n    {\n      \"repo\": \"github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes\",\n      \"path\": \"staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go\",\n      \"symbol\": \"ProcessEvents\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The Kubernetes API server implements comprehensive audit logging to track and record all requests. The audit system consists of several key components working together:\\n\\n**Request Entry Point & Initialization:**\\nThe audit system begins with two middleware filters. `WithAuditInit` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit_init.go) initializes the audit context for each request, generates or retrieves an Audit-ID from request headers, and sets it in the response. This filter runs early in the request pipeline to ensure audit context is ready for all subsequent handlers.\\n\\n**Policy Evaluation & Event Creation:**\\n`WithAudit` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go) decorates HTTP handlers with audit logging. It calls `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent` to evaluate the audit policy configuration against the current request. The audit policy is defined in a YAML file and contains rules matching requests based on users, verbs, and resources. The policy evaluator (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/checker.go::EvaluatePolicyRule) determines the audit level (None, Metadata, Request, RequestResponse) and omitted stages for each request.\\n\\n**Audit Event Context & Processing:**\\n`AuditContext` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/context.go) holds the audit event being constructed throughout the request lifecycle. It stores the event, sink, and request audit configuration. The context supports multiple processing stages: RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete, and Panic. Each stage can be processed via `ProcessEventStage` to emit the current event state to the audit sink, allowing audit backends to capture request/response boundaries.\\n\\n**Request Metadata Capture:**\\n`LogRequestMetadata` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/request.go) populates the audit event with request details including verb, URI, user information, source IPs, and resource references extracted from authorizer attributes. Helper functions like `maybeTruncateUserAgent` ensure user agents don't exceed 1024 bytes. `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` capture request and response body objects, but only when the audit level permits (Request or RequestResponse).\\n\\n**Backend Dispatch Architecture:**\\nThe `Backend` interface (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/types.go) defines how audit events are processed. The architecture supports multiple backends simultaneously through `Union` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/union.go), which allows combining log file and webhook backends. Events are dispatched through:\\n\\n1. **Truncation Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go): Wraps other backends and enforces size limits. It truncates individual audit events (removes request/response bodies if they exceed MaxEventSize) and splits batches if they exceed MaxBatchSize. Events are marked with an 'audit.k8s.io/truncated' annotation when truncation occurs.\\n\\n2. **Buffered Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Optionally buffers events before sending to the delegate backend. Supports three modes: blocking (synchronous), blocking-strict (synchronous with errors on RequestReceived stage failures), and batch (asynchronous). The batched mode accumulates events up to MaxBatchSize or MaxBatchWait duration before sending. Rate limiting can be applied via ThrottleQPS and ThrottleBurst configuration.\\n\\n3. **Log Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to a file in either legacy (text) or JSON format. Uses file rotation with configurable MaxAge, MaxBackups, and MaxSize parameters via lumberjack.\\n\\n4. **Webhook Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP. Implements retry logic that retries on any error to ensure delivery reliability.\\n\\n**Configuration & Initialization:**\\n`AuditOptions` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go) manages audit configuration including policy file path, log backend options, and webhook options. The `ApplyTo` method orchestrates the full audit setup: loading the policy file, creating the log backend (if path specified), creating the webhook backend (if config file specified), wrapping backends with truncation and batching options, and composing them into a union backend. to track and record all requests. The audit system consists of several key components working together:\\n\\n**Request Entry Point & Initialization:**\\nThe audit system begins with two middleware filters. `WithAuditInit` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit_init.go) initializes the audit context for each request, generates or retrieves an Audit-ID from request headers, and sets it in the response. This filter runs early in the request pipeline to ensure audit context is ready for all subsequent handlers.\\n\\n**Policy Evaluation & Event Creation:**\\n`WithAudit` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go) decorates HTTP handlers with audit logging. It calls `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent` to evaluate the audit policy configuration against the current request. The audit policy is defined in a YAML file and contains rules matching requests based on users, verbs, and resources. The policy evaluator (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/checker.go::EvaluatePolicyRule) determines the audit level (None, Metadata, Request, RequestResponse) and omitted stages for each request.\\n\\n**Audit Event Context & Processing:**\\n`AuditContext` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/context.go) holds the audit event being constructed throughout the request lifecycle. It stores the event, sink, and request audit configuration. The context supports multiple processing stages: RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete, and Panic. Each stage can be processed via `ProcessEventStage` to emit the current event state to the audit sink, allowing audit backends to capture request/response boundaries.\\n\\n**Request Metadata Capture:**\\n`LogRequestMetadata` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/request.go) populates the audit event with request details including verb, URI, user information, source IPs, and resource references extracted from authorizer attributes. Helper functions like `maybeTruncateUserAgent` ensure user agents don't exceed 1024 bytes. `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` capture request and response body objects, but only when the audit level permits (Request or RequestResponse).\\n\\n**Backend Dispatch Architecture:**\\nThe `Backend` interface (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/types.go) defines how audit events are processed. The architecture supports multiple backends simultaneously through `Union` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/union.go), which allows combining log file and webhook backends. Events are dispatched through:\\n\\n1. **Truncation Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go): Wraps other backends and enforces size limits. It truncates individual audit events (removes request/response bodies if they exceed MaxEventSize) and splits batches if they exceed MaxBatchSize. Events are marked with an 'audit.k8s.io/truncated' annotation when truncation occurs.\\n\\n2. **Buffered Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Optionally buffers events before sending to the delegate backend. Supports three modes: blocking (synchronous), blocking-strict (synchronous with errors on RequestReceived stage failures), and batch (asynchronous). The batched mode accumulates events up to MaxBatchSize or MaxBatchWait duration before sending. Rate limiting can be applied via ThrottleQPS and ThrottleBurst configuration.\\n\\n3. **Log Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to a file in either legacy (text) or JSON format. Uses file rotation with configurable MaxAge, MaxBackups, and MaxSize parameters via lumberjack.\\n\\n4. **Webhook Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP. Implements retry logic that retries on any error to ensure delivery reliability.\\n\\n**Configuration & Initialization:**\\n`AuditOptions` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go) manages audit configuration including policy file path, log backend options, and webhook options. The `ApplyTo` method orchestrates the full audit setup: loading the policy file, creating the log backend (if path specified), creating the webhook backend (if config file specified), wrapping backends with truncation and batching options, and composing them into a union backend. Both log and webhook backends can have independent truncation and batching configurations.\\n\\n**Policy File Format:**\\nAudit policies are loaded from YAML files using `LoadPolicyFromFile` and `LoadPolicyFromBytes` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/reader.go).   "file_path": "/workspace/answer.json",
  "new_string": "  \"text\": \"The Kubernetes API server implements comprehensive audit logging to track and record all requests. The audit system consists of several key components working together in a well-defined pipeline:\\n\\n**Request Entry Point & Initialization:**\\nThe audit system begins with two middleware filters in the HTTP handler chain. `WithAuditInit` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit_init.go) is the outermost filter that initializes the audit context for each request. It generates or retrieves an Audit-ID from request headers (using UUID if none provided), stores it in the context via `WithAuditContext`, and echoes it back in response headers. This filter runs early in the request pipeline to ensure audit context is ready for all subsequent handlers.\\n\\n**Policy Evaluation & Event Creation:**\\n`WithAudit` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go) decorates HTTP handlers with audit logging. It calls `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent` to evaluate the audit policy configuration against the current request. The policy evaluator uses `EvaluatePolicyRule` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/checker.go) to determine the audit level (None, Metadata, Request, RequestResponse) and omitted stages for each request based on policy rules matching users, verbs, resources, and namespaces.\\n\\n**Audit Event Context & Processing:**\\n`AuditContext` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/context.go) holds the audit event being constructed throughout the request lifecycle. It stores the event, sink, and request audit configuration. The context supports multiple processing stages: RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete, and Panic. Each stage can be processed via `ProcessEventStage` to emit the current event state to the audit sink, allowing audit backends to capture request/response boundaries. Annotations can be added via `AddAuditAnnotation` to capture additional context from various handlers (authentication, authorization, admission, etc.).\\n\\n**Request Metadata Capture:**\\n`LogRequestMetadata` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/request.go) populates the audit event with request details including verb, URI, user information, source IPs, and resource references extracted from authorizer attributes. Helper functions like `maybeTruncateUserAgent` ensure user agents don't exceed 1024 bytes. `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` capture request and response body objects, but only when the audit level permits (Request or RequestResponse). The admission layer uses `WithAudit` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/audit.go) to log annotations set by admission webhooks via `AddAuditAnnotationsMap`.\\n\\n**Backend Dispatch Architecture:**\\nThe `Backend` and `Sink` interfaces (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/types.go) define how audit events are processed. The `ProcessEvents` method is the core method that backends implement to handle events. The architecture supports multiple backends simultaneously through `Union` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/union.go), which allows combining log file and webhook backends into a single backend that dispatches to all configured backends. Events are dispatched through a layered chain of backends:\\n\\n1. **Truncation Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go): Wraps other backends and enforces size limits on individual events and batches. It calculates serialized event size and removes request/response bodies if they exceed MaxEventSize. If the event is still too large after truncation, it's dropped. Batches exceeding MaxBatchSize are split into smaller batches. Events are marked with an 'audit.k8s.io/truncated' annotation when truncation occurs.\\n\\n2. **Buffered Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Optionally buffers events in a channel before sending to the delegate backend. Supports three modes: blocking (synchronous ProcessEvents calls), blocking-strict (synchronous with errors on RequestReceived stage failures failing the request), and batch (asynchronous using goroutines). The batched mode accumulates events up to MaxBatchSize or MaxBatchWait duration before sending. Rate limiting can be applied via FlowControl using ThrottleQPS and ThrottleBurst configuration.\\n\\n3. **Log Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to a file in either legacy (1-line text) or JSON format. Uses file rotation (via lumberjack) with configurable MaxAge, MaxBackups, and MaxSize parameters. Each event is encoded using the appropriate encoder for the configured API group version.\\n\\n4. **Webhook Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP using GenericWebhook. Implements unconditional retry logic (retryOnError always returns true) to ensure delivery reliability. Loads webhook configuration from kubeconfig-formatted files.\\n\\n**Configuration & Initialization:**\\n`AuditOptions` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go) manages the complete audit configuration including policy file path, log backend options, and webhook options. The `ApplyTo` method orchestrates the full audit setup: loading the policy file via `LoadPolicyFromFile`, creating the log backend (if path specified), creating the webhook backend (if config file specified), wrapping backends with independent truncation and batching options, and composing them into a union backend. Configuration also defines `NewAuditTruncateOptions` with default MaxEventSize (100KB) and MaxBatchSize (10MB).\\n\\n**Policy File Format:**\\nAudit policies are loaded from YAML files using `LoadPolicyFromFile` and `LoadPolicyFromBytes` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/reader.go). The `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` creates a `policyRuleEvaluator` that evaluates policy rules by matching verbs, users, and resources. Policies define rules with matchers for users, verbs, resources, and namespaces, each specifying an audit level and optional omitted stages. OmitManagedFields can be configured at both policy and rule level.\\n\\n**Metrics & Formatting:**\\nThe system includes metrics tracking (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/metrics.go) via `ObserveEvent` and `ObservePolicyLevel` for event counts and policy level distribution. Audit events are formatted via `EventString` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/format.go) as either legacy text format or structured JSON before output. The scheme (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/scheme.go) manages serialization/deserialization of audit events.\"",

        "+  \"text\": \"The Kubernetes API server implements comprehensive audit logging to track and record all requests. The audit system consists of several key components working together in a well-defined pipeline:\\n\\n**Request Entry Point & Initialization:**\\nThe audit system begins with two middleware filters in the HTTP handler chain. `WithAuditInit` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit_init.go) is the outermost filter that initializes the audit context for each request. It generates or retrieves an Audit-ID from request headers (using UUID if none provided), stores it in the context via `WithAuditContext`, and echoes it back in response headers. This filter runs early in the request pipeline to ensure audit context is ready for all subsequent handlers.\\n\\n**Policy Evaluation & Event Creation:**\\n`WithAudit` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go) decorates HTTP handlers with audit logging. It calls `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent` to evaluate the audit policy configuration against the current request. The policy evaluator uses `EvaluatePolicyRule` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/checker.go) to determine the audit level (None, Metadata, Request, RequestResponse) and omitted stages for each request based on policy rules matching users, verbs, resources, and namespaces.\\n\\n**Audit Event Context & Processing:**\\n`AuditContext` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/context.go) holds the audit event being constructed throughout the request lifecycle. It stores the event, sink, and request audit configuration. The context supports multiple processing stages: RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete, and Panic. Each stage can be processed via `ProcessEventStage` to emit the current event state to the audit sink, allowing audit backends to capture request/response boundaries. Annotations can be added via `AddAuditAnnotation` to capture additional context from various handlers (authentication, authorization, admission, etc.).\\n\\n**Request Metadata Capture:**\\n`LogRequestMetadata` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/request.go) populates the audit event with request details including verb, URI, user information, source IPs, and resource references extracted from authorizer attributes. Helper functions like `maybeTruncateUserAgent` ensure user agents don't exceed 1024 bytes. `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` capture request and response body objects, but only when the audit level permits (Request or RequestResponse). The admission layer uses `WithAudit` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/audit.go) to log annotations set by admission webhooks via `AddAuditAnnotationsMap`.\\n\\n**Backend Dispatch Architecture:**\\nThe `Backend` and `Sink` interfaces (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/types.go) define how audit events are processed. The `ProcessEvents` method is the core method that backends implement to handle events. The architecture supports multiple backends simultaneously through `Union` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/union.go), which allows combining log file and webhook backends into a single backend that dispatches to all configured backends. Events are dispatched through a layered chain of backends:\\n\\n1. **Truncation Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go): Wraps other backends and enforces size limits on individual events and batches. It calculates serialized event size and removes request/response bodies if they exceed MaxEventSize. If the event is still too large after truncation, it's dropped. Batches exceeding MaxBatchSize are split into smaller batches. Events are marked with an 'audit.k8s.io/truncated' annotation when truncation occurs.\\n\\n2. **Buffered Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Optionally buffers events in a channel before sending to the delegate backend. Supports three modes: blocking (synchronous ProcessEvents calls), blocking-strict (synchronous with errors on RequestReceived stage failures failing the request), and batch (asynchronous using goroutines). The batched mode accumulates events up to MaxBatchSize or MaxBatchWait duration before sending. Rate limiting can be applied via FlowControl using ThrottleQPS and ThrottleBurst configuration.\\n\\n3. **Log Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to a file in either legacy (1-line text) or JSON format. Uses file rotation (via lumberjack) with configurable MaxAge, MaxBackups, and MaxSize parameters. Each event is encoded using the appropriate encoder for the configured API group version.\\n\\n4. **Webhook Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP using GenericWebhook. Implements unconditional retry logic (retryOnError always returns true) to ensure delivery reliability. Loads webhook configuration from kubeconfig-formatted files.\\n\\n**Configuration & Initialization:**\\n`AuditOptions` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go) manages the complete audit configuration including policy file path, log backend options, and webhook options. The `ApplyTo` method orchestrates the full audit setup: loading the policy file via `LoadPolicyFromFile`, creating the log backend (if path specified), creating the webhook backend (if config file specified), wrapping backends with independent truncation and batching options, and composing them into a union backend. Configuration also defines `NewAuditTruncateOptions` with default MaxEventSize (100KB) and MaxBatchSize (10MB).\\n\\n**Policy File Format:**\\nAudit policies are loaded from YAML files using `LoadPolicyFromFile` and `LoadPolicyFromBytes` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/reader.go). The `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` creates a `policyRuleEvaluator` that evaluates policy rules by matching verbs, users, and resources. Policies define rules with matchers for users, verbs, resources, and namespaces, each specifying an audit level and optional omitted stages. OmitManagedFields can be configured at both policy and rule level.\\n\\n**Metrics & Formatting:**\\nThe system includes metrics tracking (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/metrics.go) via `ObserveEvent` and `ObservePolicyLevel` for event counts and policy level distribution. Audit events are formatted via `EventString` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/format.go) as either legacy text format or structured JSON before output. The scheme (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/scheme.go) manages serialization/deserialization of audit events.\"",

\"staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go\",\n      \"symbol\": \"ProcessEvents\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The Kubernetes API server implements comprehensive audit logging to track and record all requests. The audit system consists of several key components working together in a well-defined pipeline:\\n\\n**Request Entry Point & Initialization:**\\nThe audit system begins with two middleware filters in the HTTP handler chain. `WithAuditInit` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit_init.go) is the outermost filter that initializes the audit context for each request. It generates or retrieves an Audit-ID from request headers (using UUID if none provided), stores it in the context via `WithAuditContext`, and echoes it back in response headers. This filter runs early in the request pipeline to ensure audit context is ready for all subsequent handlers.\\n\\n**Policy Evaluation & Event Creation:**\\n`WithAudit` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go) decorates HTTP handlers with audit logging. It calls `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent` to evaluate the audit policy configuration against the current request. The policy evaluator uses `EvaluatePolicyRule` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/checker.go) to determine the audit level (None, Metadata, Request, RequestResponse) and omitted stages for each request based on policy rules matching users, verbs, resources, and namespaces.\\n\\n**Audit Event Context & Processing:**\\n`AuditContext` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/context.go) holds the audit event being constructed throughout the request lifecycle. It stores the event, sink, and request audit configuration. The context supports multiple processing stages: RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete, and Panic. Each stage can be processed via `ProcessEventStage` to emit the current event state to the audit sink, allowing audit backends to capture request/response boundaries. Annotations can be added via `AddAuditAnnotation` to capture additional context from various handlers (authentication, authorization, admission, etc.).\\n\\n**Request Metadata Capture:**\\n`LogRequestMetadata` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/request.go) populates the audit event with request details including verb, URI, user information, source IPs, and resource references extracted from authorizer attributes. Helper functions like `maybeTruncateUserAgent` ensure user agents don't exceed 1024 bytes. `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` capture request and response body objects, but only when the audit level permits (Request or RequestResponse). The admission layer uses `WithAudit` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/audit.go) to log annotations set by admission webhooks via `AddAuditAnnotationsMap`.\\n\\n**Backend Dispatch Architecture:**\\nThe `Backend` and `Sink` interfaces (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/types.go) define how audit events are processed. The `ProcessEvents` method is the core method that backends implement to handle events. The architecture supports multiple backends simultaneously through `Union` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/union.go), which allows combining log file and webhook backends into a single backend that dispatches to all configured backends. Events are dispatched through a layered chain of backends:\\n\\n1. **Truncation Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go): Wraps other backends and enforces size limits on individual events and batches. It calculates serialized event size and removes request/response bodies if they exceed MaxEventSize. If the event is still too large after truncation, it's dropped. Batches exceeding MaxBatchSize are split into smaller batches. Events are marked with an 'audit.k8s.io/truncated' annotation when truncation occurs.\\n\\n2. **Buffered Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Optionally buffers events in a channel before sending to the delegate backend. Supports three modes: blocking (synchronous ProcessEvents calls), blocking-strict (synchronous with errors on RequestReceived stage failures failing the request), and batch (asynchronous using goroutines). The batched mode accumulates events up to MaxBatchSize or MaxBatchWait duration before sending. Rate limiting can be applied via FlowControl using ThrottleQPS and ThrottleBurst configuration.\\n\\n3. **Log Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to a file in either legacy (1-line text) or JSON format. Uses file rotation (via lumberjack) with configurable MaxAge, MaxBackups, and MaxSize parameters. Each event is encoded using the appropriate encoder for the configured API group version.\\n\\n4. **Webhook Backend** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP using GenericWebhook. Implements unconditional retry logic (retryOnError always returns true) to ensure delivery reliability. Loads webhook configuration from kubeconfig-formatted files.\\n\\n**Configuration & Initialization:**\\n`AuditOptions` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/audit.go) manages the complete audit configuration including policy file path, log backend options, and webhook options. The `ApplyTo` method orchestrates the full audit setup: loading the policy file via `LoadPolicyFromFile`, creating the log backend (if path specified), creating the webhook backend (if config file specified), wrapping backends with independent truncation and batching options, and composing them into a union backend. Configuration also defines `NewAuditTruncateOptions` with default MaxEventSize (100KB) and MaxBatchSize (10MB).\\n\\n**Policy File Format:**\\nAudit policies are loaded from YAML files using `LoadPolicyFromFile` and `LoadPolicyFromBytes` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/policy/reader.go). The `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` creates a `policyRuleEvaluator` that evaluates policy rules by matching verbs, users, and resources. Policies define rules with matchers for users, verbs, resources, and namespaces, each specifying an audit level and optional omitted stages. OmitManagedFields can be configured at both policy and rule level.\\n\\n**Metrics & Formatting:**\\nThe system includes metrics tracking (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/metrics.go) via `ObserveEvent` and `ObservePolicyLevel` for event counts and policy level distribution. Audit events are formatted via `EventString` (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/format.go) as either legacy text format or structured JSON before output. The scheme (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/scheme.go) manages serialization/deserialization of audit events.\"\n}\n",
